At line 53-54:```javascriptpluginData.id = packageData.name;\npluginData.name = packageData.name;\n```\n\nSince the package.json is empty (`{}`), `packageData.name` will be `undefined`. So `pluginData.name` will be `undefined`. Then when `isActive()` is called with `undefined`, my validation will check if `undefined` matches the plugin pattern, which it won't, so it will throw an error.\n\nThe issue is that these mock plugins have empty package.json and plugin.json files. They're not meant to be real plugins - they're just for testing the plugin loading mechanism.\n\nThe solution is to be careful about where I add validation. I should NOT add validation to `isActive()` in the general sense, because it's called from many places where the plugin ID might not have been validated yet. Instead, I should only add validation at the entry points where an admin is providing input.\n\nLooking at the code flow:\n1. Admin calls Socket.IO API endpoint\n2. Socket.IO endpoint calls plugin function\n3. Plugin function should validate the ID\n\nThe entry points are the public API functions:\n- `Plugins.toggleActive(id)` - already has validation\n- `Plugins.toggleInstall(id, version)` - I added
